<div id="review_2413106016" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2413106016" />
    <a title="delaney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6270594-delaney"><img alt="delaney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553837637p2/6270594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2413106016?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="delaney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="delaney" href="/user/show/6270594-delaney">delaney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6270594-delaney?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2413106016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12492298764789651645">UM. NO. YES? <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1569606330i/28210518._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So I have to be honest, I thought <i>Carry On</i> had the best ending, and really, these characters were great in a standalone--it was...enough (it's never enough, my friends). Hearing that there was going to be a second book (i.e. <i>Wayward Son</i>) I thought it was unnecessary. However: I WAS OFC HAPPY TO SEE BAZ, SIMON, AND PENELOPE AGAIN. <b>BUT:</b> I was skeptical if it would be necessary. <br/><br/>UH--<br/><b>NECESSARY EVIL.</b> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1568348624ra/28140079.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I literally <i>hugged</i> this book when I finished and I wanted to go grab my copy of <i>Carry On</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12492298764789651645" style="display:none">UM. NO. YES? <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1569606330i/28210518._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So I have to be honest, I thought <i>Carry On</i> had the best ending, and really, these characters were great in a standalone--it was...enough (it's never enough, my friends). Hearing that there was going to be a second book (i.e. <i>Wayward Son</i>) I thought it was unnecessary. However: I WAS OFC HAPPY TO SEE BAZ, SIMON, AND PENELOPE AGAIN. <b>BUT:</b> I was skeptical if it would be necessary. <br><br>UH--<br><b>NECESSARY EVIL.</b> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1568348624ra/28140079.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I literally <i>hugged</i> this book when I finished and I wanted to go grab my copy of <i>Carry On</i> and reread it all over again and then go and reread <i>Wayward Son</i> all over again. <b>YEAH, THAT'S THE BEST COMPLIMENT YOU CAN GIVE A BOOK.</b> <br><br>Truthfully, the vibe in this book is definitely different from the first. There are a lot of mentions and parallels and it's still funny, but it's dark and deals more with emotions, trauma, depression, relationships...the real stuff. I did find the first to be more fanfic-y so this one felt more real to me, in a way, and I appreciated that. Seriously, I think that's why I enjoyed it so much--it gave me substance and maturity instead of just fluff, which was exactly what I needed (even though I didn't know it). <br><br>The characters are maturing and Snowbaz is not the perfect couple. They need to communicate with each other, sit down and talk without having to deal with vampire cults and magic mishaps. I always liked how REAL Rowell depicts relationships and this one, no less. The two are so used to fighting with each other and being full of magic that Simon having wings&amp;tail and being without magic while Baz is a vampire has thrown their whole dynamic in a spiral. They are still figuring things out and every time they get somewhere, they argue and fight as it is something they have always done--<b>BUT THEY STILL LOVE EACH OTHER SO, SO MUCH, AND IT'S MORE THAN JUST A CRUSH. I AM HERE FOR THE ANGST, BUT ALSO GIVE ME THE FLUFF.</b> <br><br>Simon did feel sidelined in this book...I felt that there was more exploration of Baz, which I didn't mind, I am totally here for this flammable queen and his flower outfits. But Simon is depressed, he's lost, he's traumatized and the only time he feels whole is in battle, so now he needs to learn to come home. <br><br>There is also a new character: SHEPARD. His first word from his chapter, and I quote, "Welp." YUP, you can literally pinpoint when I fell in love with this character. What a broken yet beautiful character to join the cast of other broken yet beautiful characters (Rowell is a master at making realistic characters). <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1569608594i/28210636._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I will be very, VERY SAD if Rowell does not release another book, because that ending was abrupt and I NEED SOME CLOSURE WITH SNOWBAZ. <b>URG, THEY NEED TO STILL TALK AND ONLY THEN WILL THEY UNDERSTAND EACH OTHER AND THEIR RELATIONSHIP.</b><br><br>Okay, I'll leave with a spoiler section of my favorite parts/quotes (and other stuff I think maybe spoiler-y).<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1569609782i/28210695.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>~<b>Starting the book with an epilogue and ending it with a prologue</b> is such a power move!! Like, that is literally saying Simon's end in magic and now the start in something new. LOVING the depth that isn't seen immediately, LOVING IT. <br>~Simon:"It's sitting in economy that's making us gay."<br>~Also Simon: "If I thought I looked cool behind the wheel, I wasn't prepared for Baz."<br>~Also Simon: turned on by Baz slaying vampires and gets hella jealous whenever any guy makes eyes or flirts or feels up his hot AF boyfriend. Literally tells Lamb to back off because he's my boyfriend.<br>~Also Simon: my sexuality is "Baz-only-sexual."<br>~Simon not trusting vampires, but realizing that's exactly how he fell for his boyfriend (by teaming up with the enemy, trusting the first vampire you meet, and following them into the desert). <br>~Baz's list of things he hates includes THE SUN and THE WIND as #1 &amp; #2. And special shout out to his mom's scarf (I thought he would lose it).<br>~Baz yelling at Simon that he's beautiful even though Simon didn't hear it. :'(<br>~Baz kissing Simon good night (Baz, just call him Simon :( and also tell him that you love him because you realized you haven't).<br>~Ren Faire vampire slaying<br>~CHAPTER 41 IS LITERALLY THE NEW CHAPTER 61!!! The whole part of tying hearts together is gruesome and dramatic yet so very beautiful. <br><b>"WHY CAN'T YOU SEE THAT I WOULDN'T BE HAPPY ANYWHERE WITHOUT YOU?"</b><br>(do you hear my bawling in my own tears?)<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>PRE-RELEASE REACTIONS:</b><br>WE HAVE A COVER.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1552660592l/44034303.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Baz looking hella gay and hella fine with the golden sun behind him like he's Jesus holy wow. And Simon wow in that leather jacket damn. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552707548ra/27212377.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>OMG ROAD TRIP.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1558110781l/44034303.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558330804ra/27543012.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12492298764789651645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kwmOmpTHwc8F8VLgB5CpARDVe6gMJtKoGxojxqLMccUgTw+GRX2Zn7scRhwX174kZ1ymwyfq78r4xSvo3zcJyQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Q93zUZiYhnuoYcIvsI7hExAd5399AzlOGENM944mFZvwm3JNSSLeKxaM1tOgyfY2Z5Q6FFbPBCz7nETZ891tlw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

With his intrepid sister and the Veep’s genius granddaughter, they’re the White House Trio, a beautiful millennial marketing strategy for his mother, President Ellen Claremont. International socialite duties do have downsides—namely, when photos of a confrontation with his longtime nemesis Prince Henry at a royal wedding leak to the tabloids and threaten American/British relations.\n\nThe plan for damage control: staging a fake friendship between the First Son and the Prince. Alex is busy enough handling his mother’s bloodthirsty opponents and his own political ambitions without an uptight royal slowing him down. But beneath Henry’s Prince Charming veneer, there’s a soft-hearted eccentric with a dry sense of humor and more than one ghost haunting him.\n\nAs President Claremont kicks off her reelection bid, Alex finds himself hurtling into a secret relationship with Henry that could derail the campaign and upend two nations. And Henry throws everything into question for Alex, an impulsive, charming guy who thought he knew everything: What is worth the sacrifice? How do you do all the good you can do? <span id="freeTextContainer12402541557141053768">Rainbow Rowell writes books. Sometimes she writes about adults (ATTACHMENTS and LANDLINE). Sometimes she writes about teenagers (ELEANOR & PARK, FANGIRL and THE SIMON SNOW BOOKS.). But she always writes about people who talk a lot. And people who feel like they're screwing up. And people who fall in love.<br/><br/>When she's not writing, Rainbow is reading comic books, planning Disney World trips and arguin</span>
  <span id="freeText12402541557141053768" style="display:none">Rainbow Rowell writes books. Sometimes she writes about adults (ATTACHMENTS and LANDLINE). Sometimes she writes about teenagers (ELEANOR &amp; PARK, FANGIRL and THE SIMON SNOW BOOKS.). But she always writes about people who talk a lot. And people who feel like they're screwing up. And people who fall in love.<br /><br />When she's not writing, Rainbow is reading comic books, planning Disney World trips and arguing about things that don't really matter in the big scheme of things.<br /><br />She lives in Nebraska with her husband and two sons.<br /><br />More at rainbowrowell.com.</span>
